  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ee6b0fd0-9098-47f4-9f64-2f9368f6f867'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_2423439005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2423439005" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423439005?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mermaids">mermaids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423439005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18034353839469487439">I haven’t read a mermaid story in so long I almost forgot they existed.<br/><br/>I went into this one expecting to be buried under an avalanche of cuteness, and that’s exactly what happened. <br/><br/>I’m going to tell you right off the bat that it’s childish and the main character immature as well as single-focused on getting the boy she wants, so do not pick it up if you wish for great depth and a complex world.<br/><br/>But do pick it up if you’ve missed mermaids, too, and are often entertained by teenage girls who make p</span>
  <span id="freeText18034353839469487439" style="display:none">I haven’t read a mermaid story in so long I almost forgot they existed.<br /><br />I went into this one expecting to be buried under an avalanche of cuteness, and that’s exactly what happened. <br /><br />I’m going to tell you right off the bat that it’s childish and the main character immature as well as single-focused on getting the boy she wants, so do not pick it up if you wish for great depth and a complex world.<br /><br />But do pick it up if you’ve missed mermaids, too, and are often entertained by teenage girls who make poor decisions in the department of love. <br /><br />Even the author is single-minded. Hello, there are other characters in the story, and yet they serve little to no purpose, unless it’s to support/torment Lily. They do not stand on their own.<br /><br />Fortunately, Lily grows on you, and I have to say, I wasn’t at all bothered by her love interest. Well, the second one. Yes, he acts like an alpha male sometimes – and a jerk – but I saw the good in him, and how can one not acknowledge his steaminess and undying love for Lily?<br /><br />I can’t give this book more, despite its fun content, because I don’t feel as though it’s a worthy addition to the collection of mermaid stories out there, seeing that it is predictable and under-developed, but I did find some of its elements unique, such as the idea of bonding through kisses and ‘‘challenges’’ linked to counselling required for a merperson to break a bond.<br /><br />That epilogue also got me really curious about the sequel. Nicely played. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18034353839469487439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5978806116171958850">This book is corny! In fact- a wave of sadness overcomes me when I realize the depths that this author has sunk to. Drowning her audience in a sea of underwater puns. See I can do it too!! <br/><br/>But seriously this book feels like it was written as an 11 year olds creative writing essay that just got out of hand. If the character is mean they are a sea slug if they are nice they are an angel fish. (Constantly!) It just gets ridiculous. But worst of all the characters are LAME!! <br/><br/>Lily clearly has a perse</span>
  <span id="freeText5978806116171958850" style="display:none">This book is corny! In fact- a wave of sadness overcomes me when I realize the depths that this author has sunk to. Drowning her audience in a sea of underwater puns. See I can do it too!! <br /><br />But seriously this book feels like it was written as an 11 year olds creative writing essay that just got out of hand. If the character is mean they are a sea slug if they are nice they are an angel fish. (Constantly!) It just gets ridiculous. But worst of all the characters are LAME!! <br /><br />Lily clearly has a persecution complex that is entirely unfounded in reality. She is convinced that Quince (yes like the fruit) is out to ruin her life; this is motivation for half the plot of the book and most of the whining. Of which the latter is in great supply and the former is basically non existent. Unfortunately the only evidence of Quinces "Sea slugish" ways is a very brief moment where he points out that she has lip gloss on her cheek. Oh how I wish my enemies where so cruel! <br /><br />If you are twelve have a poor vocabulary and are very, very bored jump on in, the waters just to your liking, if not then swim for cover!!</span>

<div id="review_107774664" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107774664" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107774664?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tweens and anyone in the mood for a light and sweet mermaid love tale </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=prospect-library">prospect-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107774664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12738398781897537778"><b>3.5 - 4 Stars</b> - <i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href='http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/04/forgive-my-fins-by-tera-lynn-childs.html/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i><br/><br/><i>(Plot points mentioned deal with aspects contained in the book blurb)</i><br/><br/>Is it just guppy love or a love as deep as the ocean? <br/><br/>Yes, I have been indoctrinated from all the puns in this book. ^_^ The sea puns and mermaid fish slang were a little jarring, at first, but son of swordfish (as Lily would say), once I got into the flow, I was all bubbly smiley reading them and at times even chuckling. Though I can see how the steady stream of puns co</span>
  <span id="freeText12738398781897537778" style="display:none"><b>3.5 - 4 Stars</b> - <i><b>Also reviewed at:</b> <a href="http://ladyjaynesreadingden.blogspot.com/2011/04/forgive-my-fins-by-tera-lynn-childs.html/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Jayne's Reading Den</a></i><br><br><i>(Plot points mentioned deal with aspects contained in the book blurb)</i><br><br>Is it just guppy love or a love as deep as the ocean? <br><br>Yes, I have been indoctrinated from all the puns in this book. ^_^ The sea puns and mermaid fish slang were a little jarring, at first, but son of swordfish (as Lily would say), once I got into the flow, I was all bubbly smiley reading them and at times even chuckling. Though I can see how the steady stream of puns could be annoyingly corny and induce seasickness if one wasn’t partial to them.<br><br><i>Forgive My Fins</i> is a cute, fun, quick and easy read. This is the first book I’ve read by Tera Lynn Childs. It was also my first mermaid story, other than The Little Mermaid. So, I can’t compare it to any other YA mermaid books out there, but I did like the different twist from the Little Mermaid. <br><br>Almost 18-year old Lily Sanderson, half-mermaid, half-human, has been secretly in love with Brody Bennett, swim champion, for 3 years. Quince Fletcher, on the other hand, has been nothing but an obnoxious, annoying blowfish of a biker-boy neighbour and definitely <i>NOT</i> Lily’s idea of a dream mermate.<br><br>When a case of mistaken ‘kisstaken’ identity at the Spring Fling ends up accidentally magically “bonding” Lily to Quince, Lily must reveal her secret to him and take him to her ocean home to meet Daddy dearest in the underwater kingdom of Thalassinia, to reverse this mistake of tsunami proportions. Brody is the one that Lily wants to spend happily-ever-after under the sea with! *cue Under the Sea music*<br><br>I really liked Quince, from the beginning, and his behaviour towards Lily reminded me of little boys who pull the girl they like’s pigtails to get their attention. Quince’s teasing manner, Lily’s fiery reactions to him, and him calling Lily “princess”, also reminded me of the sparks between Han Solo and Princess Leia, which I love.<br><br>One of the issues I had though, were the number of times Lily kept referring to “the bond”. I understood it was to show Lily being in denial about any attraction she was developing towards Quince, the bane of her existence, and blaming it on the effects of “the bond”, but after a while it just felt like Ms Childs was hitting the reader over the head with a baby whale with it. Ironically, the other issue I had was in relation to what I felt was a bit of a plot hole regarding mermaid bonding. <br><br>Despite those issues, however, I found myself smiling a lot reading this book, got a few yummy shivers, and definitely had a big smile on my face when I reached the end. If you are looking for a deep read then swim away from this one, but if you’re looking for something buoyant then dip your toes into this sweet and innocent tail…Oops! I mean “tale”. ^_^<br><br>(If the puns in this review annoyed you, then you should probably steer clear of <i>Forgive My Fins</i>!) <br><br>A few of my fave quotes:<br><br> <i>‘"I don't believe it,” Quince says with absolute certainty. “I don't believe anything magical can make someone more in love.” <br>He looks me right in the eye as he says, “Love is already the strongest magic in the world."’<br><br>‘"Oh, Lily," He says shaking his head. "I know about love. About wanting and dreaming and wishing with every part of your soul. I know enough to recognize the parts that are real and the parts that are only in my fantasy." He turns his head slightly to face me, and I find myself saying, "L-like what?" <br>"Like when she cries and my heart tears into little shreds, and all I can think of is making her forget the source of her sadness." His face is blank, emotionless. His words - and the underlying emotion bombarding me through the bond - more than make up for it. "That's real." <br>My voice is barely a whisper when I ask, "And fantasy?" <br>"Believing she'll ever feel the same way."<br><br>"When he pulls back, his eyes glow with the love I know is shining inside. I’m sure my eyes are glowing just as bright, because I can feel the tears of joy sliding down my cheeks.<br>For several long minutes, we just smile at each other. I’m sure we look like stupidly in love teenagers – to Aunt Rachel and whoever else happens to be watching – but we know the truth. There’s nothing stupid about it."<br><br>"Lord love a lobster, he has a beautiful chest." </i> <br>(Just had to toss that one in there! And it’s relevant to my visualisations below) LOL<br><br>My Lily (Taylor Swift):<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380336184i/694669.jpg" width="250" height="360" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380336184i/694670.jpg" width="385" height="295" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>My Quince (Cam Gigandet): <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380336184i/694671.jpg" width="400" height="295" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380336184i/694672.jpg" width="260" height="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><br><i>COPYRIGHT DISCLAIMER: I do not hold the copyright to any of the images used in this review. They are posted to add visuals to the review and for fun. If any of these images are yours and you would like me to remove them, please let me know, and I will do so as soon as possible. If I can identify the copyright, I will do so.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="12738398781897537778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_96093924" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96093924" />
    <a title="Janina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3455554-janina"><img alt="Janina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404584313p2/3455554.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96093924?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janina" href="/user/show/3455554-janina">Janina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=given-away">given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96093924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5468954777240978517">This one wasn't for me. It was somehow too … pink, girly, fluffy and cute. The story itself was very predictable, which only made me want to shake the heroine and make her see what was going on already. Her absolute cluelessness really annoyed me. <br/>And seriously, how can you be in love (and I'm referring to the I-love-you-so-much-I-want-to-marry-you-and-spend-the-rest-of-my-life-with-you kind of love here) with someone you rarely talk to and don't really know that well? I mean, having a crush, ok</span>
  <span id="freeText5468954777240978517" style="display:none">This one wasn't for me. It was somehow too … pink, girly, fluffy and cute. The story itself was very predictable, which only made me want to shake the heroine and make her see what was going on already. Her absolute cluelessness really annoyed me. <br />And seriously, how can you be in love (and I'm referring to the I-love-you-so-much-I-want-to-marry-you-and-spend-the-rest-of-my-life-with-you kind of love here) with someone you rarely talk to and don't really know that well? I mean, having a crush, okay, but dreaming of marriage and wanting to tell that person your biggest secret? Ahm, no.<br /><br />Concerning the love story concept: it is pretty common in YA literature, but I've seen it done better in other, contemporary novels (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3874811.Something__Maybe" title="Something, Maybe by Elizabeth Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Something Maybe</a> by Elizabeth Scott comes to my mind, for example).<br /><br />The underwater-world had a very disney-like feel to it, and although I don't mind watching the occasional disney movie, it's not really what I'm looking for in a book.<br /><br />This was my first real mermaid book, and it certainly won't be my last, but I'm sure that there are better ones out there.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5468954777240978517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69615392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69615392" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69615392?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1310688-kristi?shelf=signed-books">signed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69615392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13161722233705662047">Looking for a fun, quick, cute, summer read? Look no further! Forgive My Fins has it all and more!<br/><br/>Let's just say I'm head over tail for the whimsical mermaid tale!<br/><br/>Such a cute story. This is definitely a novel that will appeal to the upper ya crowd but at the same time, is something that I wouldn't hesitate to recommend to the younger ya and even mg readers.<br/><br/>I adored Quincy from the first spitball mention. Not really specifically because of the spitball, but because he seemed like the genuinely fu</span>
  <span id="freeText13161722233705662047" style="display:none">Looking for a fun, quick, cute, summer read? Look no further! Forgive My Fins has it all and more!<br /><br />Let's just say I'm head over tail for the whimsical mermaid tale!<br /><br />Such a cute story. This is definitely a novel that will appeal to the upper ya crowd but at the same time, is something that I wouldn't hesitate to recommend to the younger ya and even mg readers.<br /><br />I adored Quincy from the first spitball mention. Not really specifically because of the spitball, but because he seemed like the genuinely funny and incredibly sweet guy. Don't ask me how I got all of that out of a spitball, but I just did.<br /><br />Lily was an excellent protagonist. I was a little worried that she might come across as stuck up, since she was a princess and all, but she's incredibly humble and insecure. She might have been fishy royalty, but teen girls won't have a hard time relating to her at all!<br /><br />The novel was a bit predictable, but I still enjoyed the journey. I loved the whole bonding issue, which I don't want to get into much, since it could be potentially spoilery. But it was interesting to see how Childs invented her own mermaid mythology. Did not see that epilogue coming though, I'm hoping that may mean a sequel? One can hope anyway. And can I just say that I'm so excited to see mermaids! I've always been.<br /><br />I loved Childs' writing style in Oh. My. Gods. and was glad to see that Forgive My Fins had that signature quirky, easy style. And I'm not embarrassed to admit that I giggled uncontrollably throughout most of this novel. It was so much fun to read.<br /><br />Add this one to your summer read list!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13161722233705662047" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1198457941" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198457941" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198457941?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=nothing-special">nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=supernatural-stuff">supernatural-stuff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=no-hell-no">no-hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=mary-sue-warning">mary-sue-warning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=read-only-when-running-out-of-book">read-only-when-running-out-of-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198457941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3590949970834820849"><i>Pre-review before I finish the book</i>: I know I'm at least 12 years older than the targeted audience but still...I can and will appreciate good teenagers' dramas. However! The stupidity and immaturity of the Main Character really is not endearing (I kept rolling my eyes at a lot of things said MC had said and done)...I'd been 17 years old once and I don't think teenagers at this age are that bad. <br/><br/><i>thoughts after I'd finished reading:</i><br/><br/>This time I can't even say <i>'Oh what a great big disappointment!'</i> b</span>
  <span id="freeText3590949970834820849" style="display:none"><i>Pre-review before I finish the book</i>: I know I'm at least 12 years older than the targeted audience but still...I can and will appreciate good teenagers' dramas. However! The stupidity and immaturity of the Main Character really is not endearing (I kept rolling my eyes at a lot of things said MC had said and done)...I'd been 17 years old once and I don't think teenagers at this age are that bad. <br /><br /><i>thoughts after I'd finished reading:</i><br /><br />This time I can't even say <i>'Oh what a great big disappointment!'</i> because I'd expected this book to be sucky even before I turned the first page. Why? Because I'd already read Tera Lynn Childs' YA paranormal novels which are based on the Medusa myths, and the two books I've managed to read aren't doing great neither.<br /><br />See my short reviews for both Medusa myths retelling books here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/618197851?book_show_action=false">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/948404158?book_show_action=false">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />This time, instead of Medusa and Greek myths, we have mermaid myth and a <i>Little Mermaid</i> retelling(?) style of teenage school drama/romance drama (not my favorite genres, but I was still willing to give it a shot). <br /><br />The good things about <i>Forgive My Fins</i> are that (1) it's a quick and easy read, (2) the tone is humorous and (3) some of the romantic plots are in fact interestingly written. However, there are many flaws in the story's characters, plots and setting, those flaws just kept me rolling my eyes in disbelief:<br /><br />(1) According to the author, there's a kingdom of merfolks somewhere near the American coastline, and <b>somehow, the citizens of this ancient, magical kingdom under the sea happen to be able to all speak ENGLISH</b>. *sighs*<br /><br />(2) Lily, the female Main Character, is hopelessly stupid, boy-crazed and immature, which might have been acceptable if she's only an ordinary teenager. You see, I don't expect every single teenager to be smart and mature, but...*groans* Goodness! I'd once been a teenager but I don't remember being that clueless and stupid like Lily!<br /><br /><br />Furthermore, the real problem is,<b>somehow our main character Lily is supposed to be the heir of the kingdom of merfolks and is expected to rule the kingdom as Queen in the future</b>. <br /><br /><br />(3) the love triangle: I don't even want to go into the details... all I can say is that someone should have told Lily how silly it is to think you are going to spend the rest of your life with the first guy you had a crush on when you're 17 years old.<br /><br />(4) According to the author, there's a supposed 'rule' about mermaids/mermen can only bond with one soul mate. However, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[turns out the merfolks can break off the bond with their King's permission, yada yada. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It's not good to break the rules of your own fictional world, seriously.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I can appreciate romance dramas among teenagers *when they are well written*, I can appreciate girls who care about dresses, boyfriends and dating. I mean, there's nothing wrong about wanting to hook up with a handsome guy and daydreaming about it! However, Ms. Child doesn't have neither the writing skill nor the insight to create a meaningful, cute, light-hearted story out of the material of her own choosing. So, 1.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3590949970834820849" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_74805863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/74805863" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/74805863?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061914652" href="/book/show/6966045-forgive-my-fins">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">those who enjoyed &quot;Teenage Mermaid&quot; (Schreiber) or Ascension (Dalkey)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=high-expectations">high-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=mermaids-underwater-breathers">mermaids-underwater-breathers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=swapped-or-given-away">swapped-or-given-away</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=sequel-no-thank-you">sequel-no-thank-you</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer74805863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7851079204618708364">I rate this mermaid romance, which I have impatiently waited almost a year for, 3,5 stars altogether. It was really cute, but very predictable. In core it reminded me a lot of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3874811.Something__Maybe' title='Something, Maybe by Elizabeth Scott' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something, Maybe</a> and other <i>regular</i> YA which tell the story of a girl nursing a long time crush on a boy she doesn't really know that well. After 40 pages or so I was a tiny bit bored, but I held on tight - I was reading a <i>mermaid</i>-love-story! - and it got better again. <br/><br/>As far as <i>I-am-a-mermaid-here-is-my-story</i> books go, I l</span>
  <span id="freeText7851079204618708364" style="display:none">I rate this mermaid romance, which I have impatiently waited almost a year for, 3,5 stars altogether. It was really cute, but very predictable. In core it reminded me a lot of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3874811.Something__Maybe" title="Something, Maybe by Elizabeth Scott" rel="nofollow noopener">Something, Maybe</a> and other <i>regular</i> YA which tell the story of a girl nursing a long time crush on a boy she doesn't really know that well. After 40 pages or so I was a tiny bit bored, but I held on tight - I was reading a <i>mermaid</i>-love-story! - and it got better again. <br /><br />As far as <i>I-am-a-mermaid-here-is-my-story</i> books go, I liked both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/733809.Teenage_Mermaid" title="Teenage Mermaid by Ellen Schreiber" rel="nofollow noopener">Teenage Mermaid</a> (also predictable, because basically a retelling) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/566781.Ascension__Water_Trilogy__Book_1_" title="Ascension (Water Trilogy, Book 1) by Kara Dalkey" rel="nofollow noopener">Ascension</a>, which both offer a romantic plot, better. The last books of the Ingo-Series, especially <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1007458.The_Deep__Ingo___3_" title="The Deep (Ingo, #3) by Helen Dunmore" rel="nofollow noopener">The Deep</a>, are also far more enjoyable, if it is the underwater world and the different thinking of the merfolk the reader wants to immerge in. Forgive my Fins has some interesting explanations about underwater breathing and the tolerance of the cold ocean water, but it stongly focusses on the romance part, the emotions, the joy and pain of teenage infatuation. Be it either high school spring fling or underwater castle: The text does not offer a lot of visuals. It rather feels like skipping the landscape pictures of a slide show and getting only glimpses of beautiful things until the family pictures come into view and are to be admired and scrutinized. So if you search for the next cute teenage romance with a likable heroine and a hunky hero who hides his feelings, choregraphed in front of a wet scenery for a change, you cannot go wrong by reading <i>Forgive my Fins</i>. <br /><br />I, for my part, have decided against reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8256207.Fins_Are_Forever__Fins___2_" title="Fins Are Forever (Fins, #2) by Tera Lynn Childs" rel="nofollow noopener">Fins Are Forever</a>, though. I will await the next mermaid-themed book (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6905569.The_Forbidden_Sea" title="The Forbidden Sea by Sheila A. Nielson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forbidden Sea</a>) I have on preorder now - hoping it will offer the perfect mix (mystery, love, thrill, a believable, well-depicted underwater world) and I heartily thank Tera Lynn Childs anyway for writing a mermaid book in times that clearly favour faeries, vampires and angels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7851079204618708364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5422954624171492153">I don't think rating out of 5 stars gives enough room for judgment. <br/><br/>I prefer the standard school grading scale...Maybe a B-. <br/><br/><br/><br/>It was a light, cute, fun book! The cover is obviously stunning. I love the greens and the blues. I'm not sure what she's supposed to be blowing out of her mouth, though. Is there something I missed in the book?<br/><br/><br/><br/>Anyway, we are presented with Lily Sanderson: half-mermaid, half-human. She's nothing spectacular with her blonde hair (yay!), pale-skin, and freckles. And she's go</span>
  <span id="freeText5422954624171492153" style="display:none">I don't think rating out of 5 stars gives enough room for judgment. <br /><br />I prefer the standard school grading scale...Maybe a B-. <br /><br /><br /><br />It was a light, cute, fun book! The cover is obviously stunning. I love the greens and the blues. I'm not sure what she's supposed to be blowing out of her mouth, though. Is there something I missed in the book?<br /><br /><br /><br />Anyway, we are presented with Lily Sanderson: half-mermaid, half-human. She's nothing spectacular with her blonde hair (yay!), pale-skin, and freckles. And she's got this really annoying (see: intriguing) neighborish boy, Quince, watching her every move. Naturally, he's in love with her and sees her for the beautiful mythical creature that she is, instead of the freak she assumes to be. But she has her eyes on superjock manslut Brody, with his abundance of luscious curls and hey, he swims like Michael Phelps. Lily is convinced that he will be her mermate in life, once she kisses him with her fishy bondage-wielding lips.<br /><br /><br /><br />Lily is an okay heroine, but suffers from extreme lack of awareness. She's stubborn and naïve and insecure. I didn't love her, but she was tolerable.<br /><br /> <br /><br />Quince is my favorite character in the novel, though he comes off as quite the doormat. He's got some really cute lines though. Go Quince! Lily's obsession with Brody gets annoying and is rather unwarranted (as most high school crushes are), as there's no real chemistry between the two. <br /><br /><br /><br />The world is enjoyable, but extremely similar to that of The Little Mermaid. Trident-wielding (I realize I've used this word twice) King? Check. Secret Grotto where the light from the world above shines in? Check. I liked it, though.<br /><br /><br /><br />A solid effort from Tera Lynn Childs. There is a cliffhanger, and I'm definitely looking forward to seeing where this story goes in "Fins are Forever," due out next year.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_300514545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300514545" />
    <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda"><img alt="Jessica Buwalda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600119200p2/6926261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300514545?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Buwalda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Buwalda" href="/user/show/6926261-jessica-buwalda">Jessica Buwalda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6926261-jessica-buwalda?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300514545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10940793838045013226">I thought I was going to like this book and that it was going to be good. I never thought I would love it, read it so fast, and then start on the next in the series immediately after I put this one day. But I did. I loved it so much I think the time it took me to read it is probably up there in the top ten for record time reading.<br/>I loved that it was a tale of a fish-out-of-water (literally) who after three years has finally gotten use to the mainland and its people(so she thought) but then, when</span>
  <span id="freeText10940793838045013226" style="display:none">I thought I was going to like this book and that it was going to be good. I never thought I would love it, read it so fast, and then start on the next in the series immediately after I put this one day. But I did. I loved it so much I think the time it took me to read it is probably up there in the top ten for record time reading.<br />I loved that it was a tale of a fish-out-of-water (literally) who after three years has finally gotten use to the mainland and its people(so she thought) but then, when she is finally deciding what to do with the rest of her life and getting prepared for her role in the water life throws her a little tail spin and she spends two weeks on an adventure that changes the way she sees everything.<br />I’m so use to reading novels about a world within our own—and still on land for that matter—but I was shocked, awed, and happy to find a book about the mixture of land and sea and was curiously reading all the description of the under water land to get the picture of this beautiful kingdom.<br />Then there was the humour and emotion that filled the pages. I love when a writer can channel both of those emotions onto the page so one minute you’re rooting for her when she insults Quince and the next your laughing when he dishes out the same. She can even make getting lip gloss on a cat funny and entertaining.<br />Lily, who although is not a normal human girl, is normal enough in our society that we relate to her. We laugh with her and share the same humour and share the same experiences—although granted there aren’t a lot of us that are undercover princesses. But I think she, and of course Quince, are really what make this novel, and hopefully series, so good.<br />Good:<br />Lily—She’s funny. On top of that she’s so emotional, especially when it comes to Quince, that the emotion just radiate throughout her hair causing it to be uncontrollably frizzy and funny<br />Quince—He is my dream man. I like the guys who are rough around the edges, while be chiselled and funny, and basically gets on your nerves so much that you just want to slap him then kiss him. Then he turns around and can be the most romantic, kind, well mannered and generous person that you can’t help but look at him awe stricken. And he rides a motor cycle. *Sigh.<br />Bad: <br />It maybe could have used a little more detail about her kingdom. More about how it physically looks, the architecture, the culture, the people. <br />Overall (Writing style, story line, and general):<br />Overall I was immersed into this novel and couldn’t help it, nor did I want to. Child points out a pretty good issue especially in relation to our modern day society and that thinking that we love someone when we love them from afar. Its not really possible. I don’t believe that you can love someone without any real meaningful interaction when you actually get to know someone. And then there is the point of maybe looking even closer to home. That love might be on your neighbour’s door step.<br />Overall I found no issue with her writing style, the only thing might have been that I would have loved to have read more about her kingdom, more description of its beauty, culture and architect—it had really amazed me.<br />But, I don’t think I can really have any vital complaints. I never had to re-read something to make sense of it, or try and get her meaning out of something she wrote. It was all pretty straight forward without losing the emotion, humour or anything that really mattered. I could picture everything that happened in my mind, and exactly how all the characters actually looked. I thoroughly enjoyed this aquatic read. <br /><br />Viewer Type Recommendation:<br />If you are a mermaid lover, or someone who loves a romantic comedy (of sorts) this is one for you.<br />If you liked this you'll probably love:<br />Hush, Hush, 1-800-Where-R-U series, The Mediator Series, Jessica’s Guide to Dating on the Dark Side<br />View more of my review and others at my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com">www.mynotsovacantshelf.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10940793838045013226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_200466427" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/200466427" />
    <a title="Michelle " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4253940-michelle"><img alt="Michelle " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428021060p2/4253940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200466427?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle " href="/user/show/4253940-michelle">Michelle </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253940-michelle?shelf=review-on-blog">review-on-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4253940-michelle?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200466427" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786936585948641311">This book was beyond cute. I haven't read a good mermaid book in over a year, so I was past due for one. And this was the perfect series for me to pick up. I have already started the second book because I didn't want the story to be over when I finished the first one. I have been reading so many new adult contemporaries lately (which I still love) that it was nice to switch it up to a cute paranormal young adult book. <br/><br/>Lily is a mermaid that is living on land for a while. Her dad is king of her m</span>
  <span id="freeText8786936585948641311" style="display:none">This book was beyond cute. I haven't read a good mermaid book in over a year, so I was past due for one. And this was the perfect series for me to pick up. I have already started the second book because I didn't want the story to be over when I finished the first one. I have been reading so many new adult contemporaries lately (which I still love) that it was nice to switch it up to a cute paranormal young adult book. <br /><br />Lily is a mermaid that is living on land for a while. Her dad is king of her mer kingdom, but he seems like the most loving, most understanding dad out there. Seriously, he was great. Lily seems just like a normal girl, except she has powers, like she can affect the temperature of water and she can craft minor items of clothing and stuff like that, and she loves salty baths. Lily goes to high school where she has a crush Brody, a guy on the swim team. She also has a best friend and an annoying next door neighbor Quince. It becomes apparent pretty quickly who the real love interest was going to be but that didn't bug me. I loved Quince and even though Lily "couldn't stand him" they were still beyond adorable together. <br /><br />Lily accidentally bonds with Quince and she has to take him to her kingdom to sever the bond so she can bond with Brody. The whole book is about their adventures back and forth between land and her mer kingdom. I loved Quince. He kind of butts heads with Lily but he makes her passionate and fiery about life. I think he makes her a more lively and interesting person, or mermaid. I was so annoyed with Lily a few times when she kept making choices for the two of them. She kind of made up for it at the end but I just wanted to shake her and get her to see how great Quince was. I really liked Lily. She is responsible, and loyal and a great person. But man oh man is she stubborn. Quince gets her though, and he likes her despite all of her quirks. Lily made a decision at the end of the book that broke my heart. She kind of made up for it but I really just wanted her to go about things differently. <br /><br />What I really liked about Forgive my Fins is that it was a journey for Lily more than anyone else. I know that sounds backwards, it should be a journey for Quince since he was being introduced to a completely new world, but it was much more growth for Lily than for Quince. He seemed to take everything in stride, but Lily needed a bit of a wake up call. I loved watching her progress, and sometimes her setbacks, and I loved watching her mature and grow. Another great thing about this book is that the ending is not a cliffhanger. It can be seen as a standalone almost because the second book picks up a different plotline. Something completely new happens, but it follows the same characters. I can't wait to see where Lily and Quince will end up next! </span>
  <a data-text-id="8786936585948641311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117259865?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Valerie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Valerie" href="/user/show/1879727-valerie">Valerie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1879727-valerie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117259865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16153653042335418185">Forgive My Fins is really fast. Has a very modern setting and it's about mermaids of course. I haven't read a lot of books with mermaids (maybe one or two) so it was different, not bad, just different. <br/><br/>The premise of this book was interesting. It's easy to see where the book is headed a few chapters in but that has never fazed me. It just felt over simplified. The plot was all about breaking the bond, getting Brody, breaking the bond, getting Brody, est. Childs could at least put in <i>one</i> sub plot</span>
  <span id="freeText16153653042335418185" style="display:none">Forgive My Fins is really fast. Has a very modern setting and it's about mermaids of course. I haven't read a lot of books with mermaids (maybe one or two) so it was different, not bad, just different. <br /><br />The premise of this book was interesting. It's easy to see where the book is headed a few chapters in but that has never fazed me. It just felt over simplified. The plot was all about breaking the bond, getting Brody, breaking the bond, getting Brody, est. Childs could at least put in <i>one</i> sub plot. This book is basically a mermaid romance, I thought there would be some action but there wasn't really any. Not that there <i>has</i> to be any just expected some. <br /><br />I might've liked it better if Lily wasn't so inconsiderate and spiteful to Quince. There is innocent banter that I liked but still she rarely gives Quince the benefit of the doubt. See if Quince were a girl and I was reading it from his point of view I would think he was an idiot for giving this girl a chance from the way she treats him half the time. As it is though I liked Quince a lot and he is very sweet. Lily does redeem herself and she does the right thing in the end.<br /><br />Though I've been mostly complaining about this book I did like it. It has some funny scenes and loving ones too. Also Lily isn't all bad. I think I might try to read the second and maybe finish the series though I'll probably be at a legal drinking age by the time all the books are done.<br /><br />Just as a side note Lily has blond hair. She isn't brunette like the cover shows. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14855887429093080295">Reviewed by Jennifer Rummel for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Lily has a secret; she's a mermaid living on land due to the fact that her mother was human. Her father is king of the seas, which makes her a Thalassinian Princess. Since finding out about her mother's lineage, Lily began to understand why she doesn't feel at home in the sea.   <span id="freeText14855887429093080295" style="display:none">Reviewed by Jennifer Rummel for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Lily has a secret; she's a mermaid living on land due to the fact that her mother was human. Her father is king of the seas, which makes her a Thalassinian Princess. Since finding out about her mother's lineage, Lily began to understand why she doesn't feel at home in the sea. She moved in with her aunt and started attending Seaview High School in order to find the perfect mate.<br /><br />She's convinced she's found him. All she has to do is persuade him that she's the only girl for him.<br /><br />She better do it fast, because mermaids mate for life at a very early age. When she comes up with a plan to share her secret and the rest of her life with him, her uber-annoying neighbor foils everything.<br /><br />Now, she's forced to return home to Daddy and straighten out this huge mess, all because she kissed the wrong boy. Can she still convince her true love of her affections and hope that he returns them before her birthday?<br /><br />This mermaid story is amazing with its romantic tension, clever, snarky dialogue, secrets, and an underwater world. All of this adds up to a magical tale written by one of my favorite authors.</span>

  <span id="freeText8421397158217662684" style="display:none">Update: 2.5/5<br /><br />So I read this when I was in high school and I absolutely loved it. Now I really can't stand Lily's character. <div id="review_385185476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/385185476" />
    <a title="Miriam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10072078-miriam"><img alt="Miriam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383915365p2/10072078.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/385185476?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miriam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miriam" href="/user/show/10072078-miriam">Miriam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10072078-miriam?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10072078-miriam?shelf=1-shitty-star">1-shitty-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10072078-miriam?shelf=chick-literature">chick-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10072078-miriam?shelf=weak-heroine">weak-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10072078-miriam?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer385185476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5408805437395153307">Forgive my Fins is a painfully predictable novel, in which I guessed the plotline in less than 5 pages. It was an extremely fast read, in which nothing even had a bit of depth. Not even the <i>main</i> characters.<br/><br/>It's about a half-human/half-mermaid who lives on land and accidently gets "bonded" to the so-called obnoxious, arrogant boy next door who, SURPRISE, turns out to be her true love. A very common romance concept often daily applied to YA books.<br/><br/><u>Now straight onto the painfully unbearable characte</u></span>
  <span id="freeText5408805437395153307" style="display:none">Forgive my Fins is a painfully predictable novel, in which I guessed the plotline in less than 5 pages. It was an extremely fast read, in which nothing even had a bit of depth. Not even the <i>main</i> characters.<br><br>It's about a half-human/half-mermaid who lives on land and accidently gets "bonded" to the so-called obnoxious, arrogant boy next door who, SURPRISE, turns out to be her true love. A very common romance concept often daily applied to YA books.<br><br><u>Now straight onto the painfully unbearable characters:</u><br><br><b>Lily</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386607i/746181.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Lily</b> was an annoying heroine. She was just plain shallow and even though she's sixteen years old, still calls her father "Daddy", which most teenagers incidentally do not do in real life. Typically, she has a crush on a surfer boy, coincidentally the most popular boy in school, whom she has no chance of ever getting together because we're talking about high school here. Can it be <i>more</i> cliche?<br><br><b>Quince</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380386607i/746182._SY540_.jpg" width="260" height="331" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Quince</b> was frustrating as well,he never ever saw what Lily for she was for- an over-protected, bratty Daddy's princess who hurt him daily. Instead he just fell for her, goodness knows why, and daydreamed about her for THREE years. <br><br>Some of the characters were stereotypes stripped plain from society. Courtney for example, is the typical jealous, ex-girlfriend envious of the heroine. Brody- the typical, self-centered hottie who's the most popular boy. Dosinia- the spiteful, jealous cousin who despises the heroine. <i>Very</i> original.<br><br>Oh, and of course the puns. Oh my god, how many puns can you insert into a novel. It reached the point of inducing vomit-worthy feelings in me. All that fishy terminology was making my head ache. Don't mistake me, I have an obssessive love for puns, but there is a fine line between overusing the puns and rocking them.<br><br>All in all, I think this book could have used more angst, doesn't hurt you know, and the characters should have had a bit more depth. Not act like cardboard cut-outs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5408805437395153307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2232148611" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2232148611" />
    <a title="Danii" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41030055-danii"><img alt="Danii" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589018465p2/41030055.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2232148611?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danii" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danii" href="/user/show/41030055-danii">Danii</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2232148611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6361141588814794399">I was not a very big fan of this book.<br/>I felt like the main character was childish, immature, and just whiney. She was shallow and full headed, even when we could see that she was being an idiot. Talk about a spoiled princess!<br/>The first problem I had with this book was that Lily was so obsessed with a guy, who she had barely talked to, and when she did he sounded either stoned or just plain braindead. How in the hell could you ever like that or think he would be suitable to run the mermaid world?!</span>
  <span id="freeText6361141588814794399" style="display:none">I was not a very big fan of this book.<br />I felt like the main character was childish, immature, and just whiney. She was shallow and full headed, even when we could see that she was being an idiot. Talk about a spoiled princess!<br />The first problem I had with this book was that Lily was so obsessed with a guy, who she had barely talked to, and when she did he sounded either stoned or just plain braindead. How in the hell could you ever like that or think he would be suitable to run the mermaid world?! He could barely even talk without sounding like an idiot.<br />Second thing is that she kept pushing Quince away when she was obviously developing feelings for him, all because she somehow thinks she can get Brody, the absolute idiot I mentioned above. She just could not accept the fact, even when he was showing her how much he liked her, and in my opinion she sure as hell didn't deserve that affection from him.<br />Third thing was the tests. Where the hell did those even come from?! I feel like the author ran out of ideas and was like "Oh, I see this in books a lot, yes this is a great idea" when in reality it was stupid in this storyline. If you can't think of something that actually fits the storyline, then just stop writing it.<br />Fourth and final thing that I hated about this was that at the end, she decides that she loves Quince, after the bond is already broken, and ruins her dads goals of her becoming the queen. Shes known this since birth, and now she screws it all up because she was being shallow and just had to have the bond broken. And now her father has to find someone else to be heir, train them, and the line royal line won't be in their family anymore. GREAT JOB LILY YOU DUMB BITCH. God, and she thinks Doe is bad, when the rest of us think shes the worst.<br />Anyways, rant over. I will not be continuing this series ever. Sorry. </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378745-mary?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378745-mary?shelf=arc">arc</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144338068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6279246833036515945">**slight spoilers -- don't read after the first paragraph**<br/><br/>This is a super fast read and much like a candy bar, you are done and wondering where it all went. Well, at least this won't spend a life time on my hips. I still think about this one wistfully and how cute and sweet it is. This is just so much fun! There are so many adorable puns and cute ways Lily has about cussing -- my favorite, son of a swordfish! This is a pretty clean book with only some G rated kissing and not much else, although</span>
  <span id="freeText6279246833036515945" style="display:none">**slight spoilers -- don't read after the first paragraph**<br /><br />This is a super fast read and much like a candy bar, you are done and wondering where it all went. Well, at least this won't spend a life time on my hips. I still think about this one wistfully and how cute and sweet it is. This is just so much fun! There are so many adorable puns and cute ways Lily has about cussing -- my favorite, son of a swordfish! This is a pretty clean book with only some G rated kissing and not much else, although Lily does fantasize about it a lot. If you enjoy Kelly McClymber Salem Cheerleader series, you will really enjoy this one.<br /><br />The story introduces us to Lily Sanderson (her name is the first of many fish puns) and her life on Florida coast where she is trying to blend in with the locals even though she is a mermaid princess of Thalassinia and discover her half human side. Lily has one goal and that is to kiss the hot hunk Brody she has set her sights on to help her rule her kingdom. Of course, nothing goes according to plan and her first kiss which bonds her to the gentleman for life ends up with her annoying neighbor, Quince. <br /><br />Quince is all wrong for Lily, or so she thinks. Quince has been in love with her since he first met her, but doesn't let on. It is only when Lily explains the seriousness of that first kiss, that he truly understands what Lily is and will become. Just like any fairy tale, this one has a happy ending, but not exactly what you might think. Lily shows true maturity in realizing that she care about Quince, but can't condemn him to her lifestyle until they work their way through many issues.</span>

<div id="review_171927184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/171927184" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3959606-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287479901p2/3959606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/171927184?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/3959606-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848771345" href="/book/show/10783905-forgive-my-fins">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3959606-karen?shelf=series-to-finish">series-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer171927184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7388202113511506741">Reading Forgive my Fins was like opening the covers of a book and watching a Disney film play out in front of my eyes. It is the story of first love, crushes and friendship and it is such a cute read that I can’t see many people not loving it.<br/><br/>The main character, Lily, was really loveable and cute and she made me laugh. She has a crush on a boy at school called Brody, who in the three years she has known him has never really given her much attention, but now time is running out for Lily and she r</span>
  <span id="freeText7388202113511506741" style="display:none">Reading Forgive my Fins was like opening the covers of a book and watching a Disney film play out in front of my eyes. It is the story of first love, crushes and friendship and it is such a cute read that I can’t see many people not loving it.<br /><br />The main character, Lily, was really loveable and cute and she made me laugh. She has a crush on a boy at school called Brody, who in the three years she has known him has never really given her much attention, but now time is running out for Lily and she really needs to let Brody know of her feelings for him, like yesterday! I enjoyed reading Lily's thoughts, although I didn't always agree with her.<br /><br />Quince on the other hand, the boy next door and the bain of her life, thinks she’s making a big mistake and makes it his mission in life to get her to see that Brody just isn’t good enough for her. Lily still thinks that Quince was just put on this earth to torment the hell out of her and she’s just not having it. I thought he was an awesome character and he 'made' this book for me. He had a depth to him that I as a reader could see and was hoping that Lily would pick up on. <br /><br />I loved the chapters that Lily spent in her underwater kingdom, Thalassinia. It is described perfectly and sounds so beautiful that I wanted to go there myself. Any Mermen out there who’d like to kiss me and make me their own? No? Shame.<br /><br />I loved this book. Tera did a great job of making it a heart-warming, cute and funny read - one that I would most certainly recommend to my friends and I am looking forward to the second in the series, Fins Are Forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7388202113511506741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6458423380814715070" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book! It captured my heart from the very beginning. I’ve always loved mermaids and fantasized about castles under the sea. Forgive My Fins did not disappoint my fantasies in any area. It captured the lure and beauty of mermaids perfectly. I couldn’t get enough of the mermaid fantasy that Tera made up. I couldn’t stop smiling as I eagerly turned the pages. Lily’s and Quince’s banter amused me, and had me laughing at times. And I loved all the sea talk and slang that Lily used! This book is amazing. The sea world that Tera created is stunning, and magically beautiful. This book was such a fantastic, magical, fun read. I love, love, love it!! I cannot wait for the sequel!!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112725464?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Realteenreviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Realteenreviews" href="/user/show/3977662-realteenreviews">Realteenreviews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Terraped Humans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3977662-realteenreviews?shelf=north-stars-list">north-stars-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3977662-realteenreviews?shelf=living-destinys-list">living-destinys-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3977662-realteenreviews?shelf=dream-catchers-list">dream-catchers-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3977662-realteenreviews?shelf=we-read-it-aloud">we-read-it-aloud</a>
          </div>
